<div id="review_1885947668" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1885947668" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1885947668?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1885947668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer465576274061705523">This is exactly the sort of fantasy I love. Slow to build, but full of great ideas and fantastic world and character development. At times it reminded me a bit of Hobb's writing style (this is very high praise from me) and I really enjoyed being able to follow a character who was 35 rather than a typical 'farmboy' etc. (although we all know I love a good farmboy story too)<br/><br/>This book focuses around Cazeril, a man who has had one hell of a life. Cazeril is a war veteran at the age of just 35. He's </span>
  <span id="freeText465576274061705523" style="display:none">This is exactly the sort of fantasy I love. Slow to build, but full of great ideas and fantastic world and character development. At times it reminded me a bit of Hobb's writing style (this is very high praise from me) and I really enjoyed being able to follow a character who was 35 rather than a typical 'farmboy' etc. (although we all know I love a good farmboy story too)<br /><br />This book focuses around Cazeril, a man who has had one hell of a life. Cazeril is a war veteran at the age of just 35. He's fought for various people and at many different battle-sites. He's a thoroughly tired out man by the time we meet him travelling on the road to Chalion, but he's also a really mysterious and interesting character to try and work out. <br /><br />What I loved about this story was the depth. Starting off with a well-hardened character means Bujold allows herself to go straight into the story and to develop that and the characters as she goes. We follow Cazeril along the road where he uncovers the remnants of Death magic, and he also meets all kind of people who are both good and bad and somewhere in-between. There are lots of excellent character development scenes and thoughts I felt very pertinent to the plot. Basically i think Bujold can certainly write. <br /><br />Probably my favourite element besides the development in this book is quite a surprising thing (at least to me). I actually found myself really enjoying the political machinations we were seeing unfold. In this story Cazeril joins up to a house and starts to serve a rather powerful young lady. Whilst serving under her many of his secrets are exposed (whether he wants that or not) and he also discovers many secrets of others around him. He's a careful and clever character who has a whole load of crappy life situations to draw on for experience, and this makes him feel so much more authentic and solid as a character.<br /><br />This is a slower book for sure, but I think it really does pay off and the second half of the story really got all fired up fast. I would definitely recommend this book and I can't wait to try out the next one in this series and hopefully I will love that one even more :) 4*s from me :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="465576274061705523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_610550052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610550052" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086118-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567611029p2/4086118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/610550052?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer610550052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11140611724862115298">A highly satisfying and timeless tale of a broken hero’s recovery. Those who expect a typical sword-and-sorcery fantasy from the title or cover will be disappointed. Fans of Bujold’s sci fi Vorkosigan Saga should feel right at home with the strengths evident here: character development, world building, complex enemies, great dialogue, understated romance, and limited but well-framed episodes of violence. <br/> <br/>In a Medieval setting of competing kingdoms, the nobleman Cazaril served Chalion well in on</span>
  <span id="freeText11140611724862115298" style="display:none">A highly satisfying and timeless tale of a broken hero’s recovery. Those who expect a typical sword-and-sorcery fantasy from the title or cover will be disappointed. Fans of Bujold’s sci fi Vorkosigan Saga should feel right at home with the strengths evident here: character development, world building, complex enemies, great dialogue, understated romance, and limited but well-framed episodes of violence. <br /> <br />In a Medieval setting of competing kingdoms, the nobleman Cazaril served Chalion well in one of its wars, but was subject to treachery and ended up a galley slave for years. After escaping, he hobbles his way back to Chalion, feeling like an old man at age 35. He is saved from poverty by getting offered the job of tutor to the teenaged princess, Iselle, and older companion and cousin, Betriz. Though Chalion is at peace, Cazaril gets drawn into protecting them from impending dangers. The king is old and sickly, and a pair of evil brothers in the positions of chancellor and top general are plotting ways to make the future succession put them on top. The threat of them corrupting Iselle’s brother/prince or wangling a marriage to Iselle turns Cazaril into a hero again.<br /><br />There are no dragons or wizards or werewolves in this tale. There are, however, ghosts and living saints, and a special realization of dualism between matter and spirit. So you could call it theological fantasy. The only magic comes through special prayers and incantations made to one of the five gods worshiped in this world-- the Father, the Son, the Mother, the Daughter, and the Bastard, each with their own churches and accolytes. We only deal with one form of magic, the death spell, revealed in the first pages of the book in Carzaril’s discovery of the body of someone who cast one. The main premise of the book is that some inequality of souls taken in a critical use of the death spell in Chalion’s history that has led to a curse on the royal family. How to reverse this curse is Cazaril’s second challenge in this tale. <br /><br />The reader comes to recognize a third challenge: how can Cazaril fulfill his secret love for Betriz? Because of his health and poverty, Cazaril never believes he is a serious candidate for her hand. This could be suitable grounds for a lot of mushy stuff, but for me Bujold handles romance here in her usual masterly way. By making it more of an underground river, providing a tender refuge for me from his travails and sensitizing my empathetic hopes.<br /><br />Humor is less prominent in this book than in other Bujold stories, but it works its way nicely into the fabric. For example, here Cazaril elicits the charm of the former queen:<br /><i>“Your granddaugher is a delightful young lady.”<br />“To a man of a certain age, Cazaril, all young ladies start to look delightful. It’s the first symptom of senility.”</i><br /><br />I was moved when learning about the origins of Cazaril’s saint-like power to bear the tasks he assumes. I will tantalize you by saying only that it has something to do with what he learned after his punishment as a galley slave when he tried to save a boy from abuse: <i>I found out that there is a place beyond fear. When the body and the mind just can’t sustain it any more.</i><br /><br />Some of the interesting theological mechanics explored in this tale remind me more of the Divine Comedy or St. Augustine than the spiritual inventions in classic fantasies such as Dune, Lord of the Rings, or Pullman and C.S. Lewis’ series. In the following excerpt, the king’s zookeeper of sacred animals, Umegat, compares the constraints on human and godly powers and the explains the role of saints: <br /><br /><i>But have you really understood how powerless the gods are when the lowest slave may exclude them from his heart? And if from his heart then from the world as well, for the gods may not reach in except through living souls. If gods could seek passage from anyone they wished, then men would be mere puppets. Only if they borrow or are given will from a willing creature, do they have a little channel through which to act. …Or …sometimes, a man may open himself to them, and let them pour through them into the world. …A saint is not a virtuous soul, but an empty one. He—or she—freely gives the gift of their will to the god. And in renouncing action, makes action possible. </i><br /><br />In sum, this fantasy doesn’t have the flash of transporting you to a totally different world like the other classics mentioned, but it is great for creating a society close to our own, but different enough to be a parallel universe. The people follow our pathway with a phase of hereditary monarchy, but plausible alternative religions develop. In this universe a few human events of mythical or miraculous proportions gain a reality. But none of this overlay is heavy and is well subjugated to the drama of compelling story. The soul searching and attempts by Cazaril to make meaning of his fate feel like a creative way to lighten his load. I loved the following example which feels like the story of Job given a Buddhist slant: <br /><br /><i>If the gods saw people’s souls but not their bodies, in mirror of the way people saw bodies but not souls, it might explain why gods were so careless of such things as appearance, or other bodily functions. Such as pain? Was pain an illusion, from the gods’ point of view? Perhaps heaven was not a place, but merely an angle of view, a vantage, a perspective.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11140611724862115298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1238511153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1238511153" />
    <a title="Para (wanderer)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17550719-para-wanderer"><img alt="Para (wanderer)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490137600p2/17550719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1238511153?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Para (wanderer)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Para (wanderer)" href="/user/show/17550719-para-wanderer">Para (wanderer)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6492981-the-curse-of-chalion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17550719-para-wanderer?shelf=healing">healing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1238511153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6254581526875663597">This is not the first time I have read this book. Not even the second. My best estimate would be about fourth or fifth – it’s simply one of those comfort reads I keep returning to again and again when I need a pick-me-up. The familiarity, the characters…it’s one of those books that never grow old and I feel I owe it at least a short review.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Any man can be kind when he is comfortable. I’d always thought kindness a trivial virtue, therefore. But when we were hungry, thirsty, sick, frightened, wi</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6254581526875663597" style="display:none">This is not the first time I have read this book. Not even the second. My best estimate would be about fourth or fifth – it’s simply one of those comfort reads I keep returning to again and again when I need a pick-me-up. The familiarity, the characters…it’s one of those books that never grow old and I feel I owe it at least a short review.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Any man can be kind when he is comfortable. I’d always thought kindness a trivial virtue, therefore. But when we were hungry, thirsty, sick, frightened, with our deaths shouting at us, in the heart of horror, you were still as unfailingly courteous as a gentleman at ease before his own hearth.</i>
</blockquote><br />After years of war followed by months spent as a galley slave, Cazaril returns to Valenda, where he served as a page when he was a boy, now a broken man. Looking for a lowly position, he is instead appointed as a secretary to the young princess (or royesse) Iselle. Though the story slowly grows more epic in scope, concerning not just Cazaril’s past, but curses, gods, and the fate of the whole kingdom, it remains personal and character-focused throughout. The pacing is rather slow and languid, but I found that it fit the story rather well.<br /><br />And Cazaril is one of the most likable characters I encountered in fantasy. He’s loyal, kind, level-headed, experienced, and no matter what life throws at him, he stays true to himself and never gives up. He’s also no longer young and struggles with various aches and pains regularly, which is somewhat unusual for a fantasy protagonist, but a welcome change. I admit I have a weakness for stories of characters who are recovering from some horrible ordeal (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/334176.The_Sparrow__The_Sparrow___1_" title="The Sparrow (The Sparrow, #1) by Mary Doria Russell" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sparrow</a>'s present day storyline hit much similar notes), but even so, I found him impossible not to like and cheer for.<br /><br />The setting is faintly Spanish-inspired, which is reflected in the titles and the names. There’s no real magic per se, but there are very real gods, including curses, blessings, and miracles related to them. And with gods and religion being one of the major themes, there’s a lot of deus ex machina and convenient coincidences. It didn’t bother me because it fit the concept well and didn’t seem out of place, but if you look for a potential deal-breakers, there you go.<br /><br /><b>Enjoyment:</b> 5/5<br /><b>Execution:</b> 5/5<br /><br /><b>Recommended to:</b> fans of character-focused fantasy, those looking for uplifting books, books that are relatively low magic, standalone epic fantasy books, and/or older protagonists<br /><b>Not recommended to:</b> fans of fast-paced stories, those who hate deus ex machina, content warning: discussion of rape (nothing on-screen)<br /><br /><i>More reviews on my blog, <a href="https://otherworldsreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">To Other Worlds.</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6254581526875663597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2212721602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2212721602" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212721602?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061793042" href="/book/show/10140600-the-curse-of-chalion">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212721602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16874111730418841232"><b>“How strangely we are blinded by the surfaces of things.”</b><br/><br/>What is a diamond? A lump of ordinary coal that took pressure exceptionally well. Castillar Lupe dy Cazaril is your diamond in this story. And please do not call him broken, there is nothing broken about the diamond, even before it is cut to gain the proper shine and brilliance. <br/><br/>The Curse of Chalion is <b>a story told from the margins</b> of a great power play. You know all these books sporting princes and princesses fighting for or defending the</span>
  <span id="freeText16874111730418841232" style="display:none"><b>“How strangely we are blinded by the surfaces of things.”</b><br /><br />What is a diamond? A lump of ordinary coal that took pressure exceptionally well. Castillar Lupe dy Cazaril is your diamond in this story. And please do not call him broken, there is nothing broken about the diamond, even before it is cut to gain the proper shine and brilliance. <br /><br />The Curse of Chalion is <b>a story told from the margins</b> of a great power play. You know all these books sporting princes and princesses fighting for or defending their heritage, the tales that take you right there to the very heart of what is happening and let you experience the heat of events through the eyes and hearts, and souls of the high and lofty? This is not one these books. The tide of the tale takes us in, but we follow its erratic swirls observing them from the point of view of a seemingly unimportant shell snatched from the shore. <b>The narrator is merely a faithful companion to the main players</b>. Furthermore, <b>the story, as all good stories should, unfolds in both directions, into the future and into the past - not retrospectively, but in a way that allows the reader to make sense of seemingly unimportant events or to join them into a meaningful sequence</b>. <br /><br /><i>“Sec’t’y-tutor, One ea. Gift from Grandmama. Aged thirty-five. Badly damaged in shipping”.</i><br /><br />In spite of his lowly status, <b>Caz is the main pillar of the story</b>. In fact, he bears the weight of the whole book on his weary shoulders. <b>I was genuinely surprised how this middle-aged man was able to hook me into his narrative</b>. Ex-soldier turned secretary whose main ambition was to find a quiet corner where high life would not bother him anymore does not sound terribly exciting, does it? And yet, this steadfast and principled, rather introvert person, swept into the drama shows that the smallest piece of rock can start a huge avalanche and be a crucial agent of momentous change. Caz is not a mere instrument, an accidental tool or a passive witness, he reaches out into the thickest of the forces at play to grasp and to master what is happening. This ownership is rooted in the free will of a stellar character:<br /><br /><i>“Events may be horrible or inescapable. Men always have a choice - if not whether, then how, they may endure.”</i><br /><br />Caz, whose <b>body has been mutilated but his spirit is not broken, and at times it soars so high that hardly any other character in the book can equal these heights,</b> endures without becoming a pompous martyr. <br /><br />The motif I found the most profound in the whole book is <b>the invitation to reconsider our own personal paths</b> - when we a arrive at some point in our lives we can always <b>ask ourselves: was it by accident, by pure chance or was there some design, some pattern to it? If so, where and when has it begun?</b> Was I a conscious and willing element or just a grain of sand caught in the turning gyres? From this vantage point, Caz’s journey is simply incredible and wonderfully told. <br /><br /><b>In addition to lovely prose, Ms Bujold created a cohort of engaging characters</b>. The members of the ruling House of Chalion, including its youngest scions, the siblings Royesse Iselle and Royse Teidez, two focal points of the intrigue, the courtiers, the servants, even the animals and the divine beings, form an amazing assortment of tropes and figures. <br /><br /><i>“The god’s most savage curses come to us as answers to our own prayers. Prayer is a dangerous business. I think it should be outlawed.”</i><br /><br />Undoubtedly, the way Ms Bujold approached the divine and supernatural is one of the strongest points of the book. She tackled this theme at least as skilfully as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2916869.Robert_Jackson_Bennett" title="Robert Jackson Bennett" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jackson Bennett</a> in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2011586768?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Divine Cities</a> and much, much better than the (unjustifiably, if you ask me) acclaimed Greatcoats by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7390210.Sebastien_de_Castell" title="Sebastien de Castell" rel="nofollow noopener">Sebastien de Castell</a> (although Saint's Blood is still ahead of me, so perhaps I'm in for a pleasant surprise). <br /><br /><b>The whole idea of a curse, central to the whole plot was fiendishly clever</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[distorting and betraying virtues and turning good into evil <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> because it rendered evil characters with more than a two-dimensional perspective, <b>even though the majority of what happens is quite easy to surmise in advance</b>.<br /><br />On the (relative) cons side, the <b>pacing is slow</b> and filled with intrigue rather than action (please note, it was not an issue for me, I couldn't put the book down) and the <b>romantic subplot is entirely unromantic</b> (and not because of the age difference, but due to a total lack of chemistry). <br /><br />I have found in Bujold everything I have been looking for and even more than I asked, and I will definitely be continuing the series and reading her other novels.<br /><br />-- <br />Also in the series: <br /><br />2. Paladin of souls RTC<br />3. The Hallowed Hunt RTC</span>
  <a data-text-id="16874111730418841232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349493115?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780380818600" href="/book/show/395967.The_Curse_of_Chalion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>,

<div id="review_1886264161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1886264161" />
    <a title="Allison Hurd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd"><img alt="Allison Hurd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530670583p2/14495279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1886264161?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Hurd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Hurd" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd">Allison Hurd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fem-author">fem-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1886264161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12822487689599541280">A sweet story of courtly intrigue and women ordering a world that thinks it's ordering them.<br/><br/><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: (no actual spoilers, just a list of topics) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ discussion of rape, child abuse, torture, domestic violence, slavery--though none on screen. Animals killed. Some gore.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><u>Things to love:</u><br/><br/>-<b>Cazaril</b>. The main character is tragically tormented, and we watch him heal. He's loyal, kind, intelligent, and extremely brave.<br/><br/>-<b>The other characters</b>. The Provencara, Iselle, Betri</span>
  <span id="freeText12822487689599541280" style="display:none">A sweet story of courtly intrigue and women ordering a world that thinks it's ordering them.<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: (no actual spoilers, just a list of topics) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ discussion of rape, child abuse, torture, domestic violence, slavery--though none on screen. Animals killed. Some gore.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Things to love:</u><br /><br />-<b>Cazaril</b>. The main character is tragically tormented, and we watch him heal. He's loyal, kind, intelligent, and extremely brave.<br /><br />-<b>The other characters</b>. The Provencara, Iselle, Betriz, Pally, the Fox, Bergen, Umegat... they all became friends. They all have lovely, distinct personalities and humors. You cheer for all of them.<br /><br />-<b>The ending</b>. I've been reading a lot of very depressing books lately. Sure, this had some darkness to it, but it was nice for everything to come to rest, and to rest happily for the principle parties.<br /><br /><u>Things I didn't love:</u><br /><br />-<b>What moves the story</b>. Caz is great. And he did marvelous things. But I'm not entirely sure why, and it feels like most of the story was actually Iselle's, Ista's, the Royina, and the other women. But this was framed as a sort of swashbuckling story and therefore, despite their own inner strengths and the fact that it was they who moved pawns, it still couldn't be their story.<br /><br />-<b>He thought Betriz was 16</b>. I get that this is loosely based upon a tale of the actual Spanish aristocracy. But it was veeery loose. I'm always a little grumbly about romances set up between people of vastly disparate ages and experiences--especially when it turns out that the person seems <i>younger</i> than their years, rather than older. This one is better than most but I still want to know what it is that makes authors write these stories.<br /><br />-<b>A bit convoluted</b>. In the manner of those gothic romances, there's a lot going on that manages to get wrapped up very neatly. It was a fun story and well told, so it's not like it hindered things, but at the end I asked "how is this all possible?" Even with the logic of the book, the plot didn't quite add up.<br /><br />-<b>Needed more magic</b>. This world has very potent magic. But apparently one god is much more direct than the others. I'd liked to have seen more about that.<br /><br />-<b>Audiobook</b>. I listened to this and a lot of it was very good but there was a lot of stuttering and laughing that felt unnecessary, and the inflection was often not how I envisioned things. It really marred some of the humor.<br /><br />Probably closer to 3.5 stars, and possibly would have been rounded up if I'd read it with my eyes or with more distance from another book that involved disparate power dynamics in a relationship. If you're looking for a sweet, action-filled romance, this would fit the bill admirably.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12822487689599541280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_331621667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331621667" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331621667?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780060097073" href="/book/show/1671467.The_Curse_of_Chalion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=squeamish-alert">squeamish-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=published-2000s">published-2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=quests">quests</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-companion-novels">series-companion-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=award-winner">award-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=clever-characters">clever-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331621667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer759082423072578251"><i>The Curse of Chalion</i> is the story of a noble, broken man who has just managed to escape from slavery. Once a soldier and a lord, Cazaril is now almost to the end of his rope, destitute, friendless, and betrayed. The first part of the book is the story of how he rebuilds his life, and how his sense of honor brings him to continue giving his life and loyalty to Chalion even when he feels he has nothing left to give.<br/><br/>It's a slow start - I didn't see what the point of it all was for quite a while. Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText759082423072578251" style="display:none"><i>The Curse of Chalion</i> is the story of a noble, broken man who has just managed to escape from slavery. Once a soldier and a lord, Cazaril is now almost to the end of his rope, destitute, friendless, and betrayed. The first part of the book is the story of how he rebuilds his life, and how his sense of honor brings him to continue giving his life and loyalty to Chalion even when he feels he has nothing left to give.<br /><br />It's a slow start - I didn't see what the point of it all was for quite a while. Cazaril is a noble sort of hero with some middle-aged wisdom to give in the role of mentor and adviser, and he is also humble. He really doesn't have any flaws, and I liked him for it - it's kind of refreshing these days. But aside from him getting sucked back into politics, it doesn't feel like it's going anywhere. <br /><br />There's a lot of groundwork-laying until about 180 pages in when something significant finally happens. From that point on, it doesn't slow down at all. It turns out to be really great fantasy with plenty of political intrigue, action, and interesting magic. Suddenly I was completely in its grip! The ending is completely satisfying, bringing together pieces that I didn't even know were part of the puzzle.<br /><br />The reason I can only give this 4 stars is that there are some gruesome parts that turned me off. Gruesome more in the lingering medical condition sense than the fleeting battle blood-and-guts sense (which I'm fine with). I'm kind of squeamish on the medical stuff though, and I really couldn't get past it, even though the rest of the story was fantastic. The slow start is something I can deal with because it pays off in the second half of the book - but give me too many medical details and I'm just not happy. That's me, though. <br /><br />This is the first book in a trilogy, but it really feels complete to me as it is. I don't feel any lingering questions forcing me to pick up the next book. It can totally stand alone if you're not in the mood for a series. From what I've read, the next book moves to one of the minor characters, so it's almost more of a companion novel. I do intend to read on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="759082423072578251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer3845025086187630826">What a great book!<br/>It reminded me to put everything by Bujold that I haven't read on my wishlist!<br/>Engaging characters meet an action-filled plot with tons of plotting and intrigue. I have to admit that this kind of "castle intrigue" is definitely one of my favorite genres of novels. I'd very much recommend this to fans of George R.R. Martin and Guy Gavriel Kay.<br/><br/>My edition came with blurbs from Robert Jordan & Dennis McKiernan, and an ad for the latest Weis & Hickman - all of which, I must admit, I </span>
  <span id="freeText3845025086187630826" style="display:none">What a great book!<br />It reminded me to put everything by Bujold that I haven't read on my wishlist!<br />Engaging characters meet an action-filled plot with tons of plotting and intrigue. I have to admit that this kind of "castle intrigue" is definitely one of my favorite genres of novels. I'd very much recommend this to fans of George R.R. Martin and Guy Gavriel Kay.<br /><br />My edition came with blurbs from Robert Jordan &amp; Dennis McKiernan, and an ad for the latest Weis &amp; Hickman - all of which, I must admit, I eyed with trepidation, not having an overly high opinion of any of those authors - but although this is undeniably epic fantasy, Bujold's writing far exceeds those other authors. I read the first chapter on my way to work - and after just that one chapter, the main character stayed in my head all day - I couldn't wait to read more. And today at work, I must admit, I had the book at my desk, sneaking a page here and there at opportune moments.... wink.gif<br /><br />Cazaril, a high-born military man who, through an act of treachery, was sold as a galley slave, has finally escaped - but barely with his life. He comes crawling back to the great house where he was employed in his youth - and, unexpectedly, finds himself in the position of tutor to a young princess, Iselle, and her handmaiden Betriz. This seemingly peaceful job may entail more than one might expect, however, considering the chaotic state of politics both within and without the kingdom of Chalion - and an evil curse that hangs over the royal family. </span>

<div id="review_1119119905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1119119905" />
    <a title="Megan Baxter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5742086-megan-baxter"><img alt="Megan Baxter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310153693p2/5742086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1119119905?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Baxter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Baxter" href="/user/show/5742086-megan-baxter">Megan Baxter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1119119905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7790352539191266942">I realized something as I was reading this book. Many fantasy books, when they involve any kind of court culture, have as their viewpoint character someone who doesn't know how it works, and blunders around until he or she figures it out. It's relatively rare to have the main character be someone who does know exactly how things work. Cazaril, the main character, is such a man. He isn't a quintessential courtier by any means, but he knows how things work.<br/><br/>Note: The rest of this review has been wi</span>
  <span id="freeText7790352539191266942" style="display:none">I realized something as I was reading this book. Many fantasy books, when they involve any kind of court culture, have as their viewpoint character someone who doesn't know how it works, and blunders around until he or she figures it out. It's relatively rare to have the main character be someone who does know exactly how things work. Cazaril, the main character, is such a man. He isn't a quintessential courtier by any means, but he knows how things work.<br /><br />Note: The rest of this review has been withdrawn due to the changes in Goodreads policy and enforcement. You can read why I came to this decision <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/349383-goodreads-this-is-not-okay?chapter=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />In the meantime, you can read the entire review at <a href="http://smorgasbook.blogspot.ca/2015/01/the-curse-of-chalion-by-lois-mcmaster.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Smorgasbook</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7790352539191266942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780380979011" href="/book/show/1142011.The_Curse_of_Chalion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer675578276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11023399119263099435"><b>Executive Summary:</b> It took me a little bit to warm up to, but in the end I found this an enjoyable read.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I read this as the August pick for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sword & Laser</a>. Despite considering myself more Sword than Laser (or maybe because I do?), I think overall I've been mostly disappointed with the Sword picks, especially the last two.<br/><br/>This one however, did not disapoint. It starts a bit slow. The pacing reminded me a bit of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_' title='Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb' rel='nofollow noopener'>Assassin's Apprentice</a>, so you if you enjoyed those books, you may enjoy t</span>
  <span id="freeText11023399119263099435" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> It took me a little bit to warm up to, but in the end I found this an enjoyable read.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I read this as the August pick for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/4170-the-sword-and-laser" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword &amp; Laser</a>. Despite considering myself more Sword than Laser (or maybe because I do?), I think overall I've been mostly disappointed with the Sword picks, especially the last two.<br /><br />This one however, did not disapoint. It starts a bit slow. The pacing reminded me a bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45107.Assassin_s_Apprentice__Farseer_Trilogy___1_" title="Assassin's Apprentice (Farseer Trilogy, #1) by Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Assassin's Apprentice</a>, so you if you enjoyed those books, you may enjoy this as well.<br /><br />Cazaril is not your typical fantasy protagonist. He's in his mid 30s for one. In fact this book doesn't feel like a fantasy book at all for most of it. There are no dragons, or wizards, or (insert your favorite fantasy race) to speak of. There does end up being magic however. And Gods of great power.<br /><br />Mostly however, this is a political story with a medieval setting. The characters are well written and interesting. Large parts of the plot are rather predictable, but that's not always a bad thing. It's the characters that make this book enjoyable.<br /><br />It's also nice to get away from all the grimdark fantasy I've been reading with something lighter. There are certainly some awful things that happen/described in this book, but nothing to the level of Song of Ice and Fire, Malazen, etc.<br /><br />Despite being listed as Chalion, #1 by good reads, this is a stand alone story. My understanding is it is actually 3 stand alone stories set in the same world. <br /><br />That is both a nice change from most fantasy these days, and a little sad, because I've grown attached to her characters and would like to see how they make out after the story ends.<br /><br />This is my first book by Ms. McMaster Bujold, but won't be my last. I at least plan to check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61904.Paladin_of_Souls__Chalion___2_" title="Paladin of Souls (Chalion, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Paladin of Souls</a>.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680037481" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5079388481102053541">What a delightful world. The work that went into researching medieval Spain sows, as does theincrediblemimagination that went into turning the story into its own consistent telling rather than just a metaphor. Now layer on top of that a deep theological debate nested in an other-worldly system where the debate is not between monotheistic beliefs and their prophets, but polytheistic beliefs and the acceptance or rejection of a lucifer-like god as a force for good or ill. Top it all off with stron</span>
  <span id="freeText5079388481102053541" style="display:none">What a delightful world. The work that went into researching medieval Spain sows, as does theincrediblemimagination that went into turning the story into its own consistent telling rather than just a metaphor. Now layer on top of that a deep theological debate nested in an other-worldly system where the debate is not between monotheistic beliefs and their prophets, but polytheistic beliefs and the acceptance or rejection of a lucifer-like god as a force for good or ill. Top it all off with strong likable characters prevailing against the odds to save a kingdom a family and a world and you have a masterwork. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5079388481102053541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_253341121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253341121" />
    <a title="Pauline Ross" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3321575-pauline-ross"><img alt="Pauline Ross" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442980323p2/3321575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253341121?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pauline Ross" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pauline Ross" href="/user/show/3321575-pauline-ross">Pauline Ross</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3321575-pauline-ross?shelf=year-2014">year-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3321575-pauline-ross?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3321575-pauline-ross?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3321575-pauline-ross?shelf=price-gift">price-gift</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253341121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15757705289266055317">I don’t know what anyone else looks for in their fantasy, but for me the number one requirement is characters I care about. This is hard to define, of course; I can’t describe what it is that creates emotional engagement in that way (if I could, I’d bottle it and sell it), but I know it when I see it.<br/><br/>And Cazaril is it, indubitably and without question. From the moment he walks onstage in his rags on page 1, he is a man I care deeply about, someone I’m rooting for all the way. He’s not great hero</span>
  <span id="freeText15757705289266055317" style="display:none">I don’t know what anyone else looks for in their fantasy, but for me the number one requirement is characters I care about. This is hard to define, of course; I can’t describe what it is that creates emotional engagement in that way (if I could, I’d bottle it and sell it), but I know it when I see it.<br /><br />And Cazaril is it, indubitably and without question. From the moment he walks onstage in his rags on page 1, he is a man I care deeply about, someone I’m rooting for all the way. He’s not great hero material (almost everything he’s been involved in seems to have gone wrong), he’s rarely called upon to wield a sword and he’s ill for most of the book, but he is a towering character of a kind that’s regrettably rare in all fiction, not just fantasy.<br /><br />The other characters are fully rounded personalities, too. The princess who doesn’t like being manipulated and decides to take control of her fate. The handmaiden who doesn’t angst when rejected, but quietly waits for her moment. The mad woman who turns out to be far more interesting than that description would suggest. And the villains who are just as much tragic victims of their fate as anyone else. And hallelujah for that.<br /><br />It’s curious that in many ways the characters fall into traditional fantasy stereotypes: the battle-weary warrior; the feisty princess about to be forced into an unwelcome marriage; the playboy prince; the evil advisor to the king. And so on. And yet they never felt in the least bit stereotypical, to me. Nor were their actions ever predictable. <br /><br />The plot centres on returning warrior Cazaril, still recovering after being betrayed into slavery, and looking for work where he was previously employed as a page. To his surprise, he’s given the job of tutor/secretary to lively princess Iselle and her companion Betriz, and then accompanies them to the royal court with all its intrigues. From there, things roll along nicely, and only one stupendous coincidence near the end rocked the credibility somewhat. This is not a high-action tale, and most of the tension comes from the history (read: enmity) between Cazaril and the man who betrayed him. I liked very much that Cazaril isn’t hell-bent on revenge, though, and just wants to keep his head down and survive as best he can.<br />The magic is low-key, and revolves around the five gods, the Father, Mother, Son, Daughter and Bastard, and the way they interact with their human followers. I’m not normally a big fan of god intervention, but maybe that’s because few authors execute the idea as well as it’s done here.<br /><br />What didn’t I like? The names, for one thing. If you’re going to have a traditional monarchy, it’s just as easy to call the participants king, queen, prince, princess, etc. Inventing all-too-similar terms like roya, royina, royse and royesse is just downright confusing. And if the titles are bad, the character names are worse: how are you supposed to pronounce Teidez and Betriz, anyway? I kept wanting to call them Tiddles and Beetroot. Then there’s the romance, which all felt ever so slightly perfunctory.<br /><br />But truly my quibbles were few and minor. This is a beautifully written book, with a memorable and wonderful main character, a plot that doesn’t depend on villains who are evil just because, and a resonant ending which brought me to tears. It’s not a sword-waving type of book, depending more on dialogue and reason to drive things forward. And I absolutely loved the saints who fell on each other with glee (there’s someone else like me! How is it for you?) and the long, detailed and gloriously funny theological debates (which is not something I ever thought to write). Highly recommended. Five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15757705289266055317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YK0Hd3U97thmDCLZrJIfqZVf4EJJiYPXNrVx1IL/Q10wwNAyFRy6/huyPZ+WPloTM4oim26v+jdJVmOGXe3WIw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hT5AB+4cC3G9hgPkcWwKaUfkJuOhWnoJVQGRjlD0KHjVU5dCjj1fV8A4HKJLwE/T4THkOoZ8A+kq4oPcj+a9Bg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13057541758170183294">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText13057541758170183294" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
